  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5e724f61-1f87-40ef-a0bc-024fe32cd428'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12296028737416175927">A New York Times best-seller!<br/><br/>"Every one of these cartoons is just something that drifted into my head when I was alone with my thoughts. And, for better or worse, I 'jotted' them down. It was only later, when perhaps I received an angry letter from someone, that it struck me: Hey! Someone's been reading my diary!"<br/><br/>Gary Larson, from the preface to The Complete Far Side<br/><br/>Revere</span>
  <span id="freeText12296028737416175927" style="display:none">A New York Times best-seller!<br /><br />"Every one of these cartoons is just something that drifted into my head when I was alone with my thoughts. And, for better or worse, I 'jotted' them down. It was only later, when perhaps I received an angry letter from someone, that it struck me: Hey! Someone's been reading my diary!"<br /><br />Gary Larson, from the preface to The Complete Far Side<br /><br />Revered by its fans as the funniest, most original, most "What the ... ?"-inspiring cartoon ever, The Far Side® debuted in January 1980 and enjoyed an illustrious 14 years on the worlds comics pages until Gary Larson's retirement in 1994. <br /><br />The Complete Far Side celebrates Gary's twisted, irreverent genius in this ultimate Far Side book, a lavish production, which takes its place alongside collector's-edition art books.<br /><br />A masterpiece of comic brilliance, The Complete Far Side contains every Far Side cartoon ever syndicated over 4,000 if you must know presented in (more or less) chronological order by year of publication, with more than 1,100 that<br />have never before appeared in a book. Also included are additional Far Side cartoons Larson created after<br />his retirement: 13 that appeared in the last Far Side book, <br />Last Chapter and Worse, and six cartoons that periodically ran as a special feature in The New York Times Science Times section as The Far Side of Science.<br /><br />Creator Gary Larson offers a rare glimpse into the mind of <i>The Far Side</i>®in quirky and thoughtful introductions to each of the 14 chapters. Complaint letters, fan letters, and queries from puzzled readers appear alongside some of the more provocative or elusive panels. Actor, author,and comedian Steve Martin offers his pithy thoughts in a foreword, and Gary<br />Larson's former editor describes what it was like to be "the guy who could explain every Far Side cartoon."<br /><br /><i>The Complete Far Side</i> © 2003 by FarWorks, Inc. All Rights Reserved. <br /><i>The Far Side</i> ® and the <i>Larson</i> ® signature <br />are registered trademarks of FarWorks, Inc.</span>

      </div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_578').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_221131714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221131714" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221131714?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=on-deck-next">on-deck-next</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=humor-and-satire">humor-and-satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1980-1989">1980-1989</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1990-1999">1990-1999</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=collected-works-of">collected-works-of</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221131714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1560166551517484245">Gary Larson’s <b>Far Side</b> was pure <b>MAGIC</b>...<br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&current=farsidewaxmanv2.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711827.jpg' alt='farsidewaxmanv2' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a>...and when it burst on the scene like a <b>talking, cow-shaped comet</b> in 1980, the strip was like nothing the newspaper funnies had ever seen. <a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&current=Penguinv2.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711828.jpg' alt='Penguinv2' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>While its single panel format and light-hearted depiction of awkward social situations and shared pain bore some resemblance to earlier comics like <i>Ziggy</i> and Larson’s own <i>Nature’s Way</i>, <b>The Far Side</b> was an anthropomorphic animal all its own, and dominated the public’s consciousness for the decade and a half that</span>
  <span id="freeText1560166551517484245" style="display:none">Gary Larson’s <b>Far Side</b> was pure <b>MAGIC</b>...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=farsidewaxmanv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711827.jpg" alt="farsidewaxmanv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>...and when it burst on the scene like a <b>talking, cow-shaped comet</b> in 1980, the strip was like nothing the newspaper funnies had ever seen. <a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=Penguinv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711828.jpg" alt="Penguinv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>While its single panel format and light-hearted depiction of awkward social situations and shared pain bore some resemblance to earlier comics like <i>Ziggy</i> and Larson’s own <i>Nature’s Way</i>, <b>The Far Side</b> was an anthropomorphic animal all its own, and dominated the public’s consciousness for the decade and a half that it was being produced. <br><br>Its unpretentious, surrealistic humor had broad appeal and could be enjoyed on multiple levels. At times, it was silly and sweet and designed simply to spread smiles. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=FSsheep-dipv2-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711829.jpg" alt="FSsheep-dipv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>Other times, the humor had such a cleverness to it that the smiles didn’t simply spread so much as explode across the reader’s face. <a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=GaryLarson-EarlyMicroscopev2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711830.jpg" alt="GaryLarson-EarlyMicroscopev2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=dolphinsBWv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711831.jpg" alt="dolphinsBWv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=FarSideGiftedSchoolv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711832.jpg" alt="FarSideGiftedSchoolv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Larson’s genius knew no sacred cows, and he probed and needled at just about everything. Whether providing insight into the meaning of life, by depicting God as an over adventuress chef...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=godjerksv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711833.jpg" alt="god jerksv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>...or using absurd juxtaposition to subtly show the marriage between big business and the war.** <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=Vikings-businessv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711834.jpg" alt="Vikings-businessv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>** This interpretation is probably a bit of a stretch, but it does seem to fit</i>.<br><br>In addition, Larson used his talking nature and human/animal relationship reversals to highlight those little moments in life that everyone could relate to...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=Larrys_Deer_Gutv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711835.jpg" alt="Larrys_Deer_Gutv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=awev2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711836.jpg" alt="awev2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>And sometimes, he was just a lunatic jokester casting a bizarre-filtered folk wisdom or pop philosophy in a comedic, fell good light...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=curiosity_killed_these_catsv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711837.jpg" alt="curiosity_killed_these_catsv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=vacuumv2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711838.jpg" alt="vacuumv2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But always...always, there was humor. Larson’s work was beloved for its blending or humor and satire with a sense of genuine warmth. Even when poking fun or envisioning catastrophe, his work never seemed pessimistic, and there was just something oddly comforting about Larson’s skewed view of the world that warmed the cockles and made you feel good. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_m2a8eh2dnt1rrylt5o1_500v2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711839.jpg" alt="tumblr_m2a8eh2dnt1rrylt5o1_500v2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Far%20side/?action=view&amp;current=357451e9-1v2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360920i/711840.jpg" alt="357451e9-1v2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I can’t tell you how many hours I spent replenishing my stores of good will perusing Larson’s work. So, after re-visiting his singular work in this massive, uber collection of his complete catalog, I thought I would share the love and try to bring a few moments of bright into your Sunday (and whatever additional days I eventually float this review). <br><br>Hope it brings a smile. <br><br>5.0 stars. HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!<br></span>

<div id="review_333284629" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333284629" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333284629?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333284629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17662591480732151455"><br/>This is the best collection of Gary Larson's artwork simply because it includes (almost) every single one of the daily syndicated comics that he penned over the years, from 1980 to 1994. As a bonus, the reader gets posters and yearly introductions from the author, detailing the creative process, the source of inspiration and wacky anecdotes related to the series. I've spaced out my lecture over almost a whole year, in order to prolong the pleasure and avoid 'overeating' a favourite 'dish', yet t</span>
  <span id="freeText17662591480732151455" style="display:none"><br />This is the best collection of Gary Larson's artwork simply because it includes (almost) every single one of the daily syndicated comics that he penned over the years, from 1980 to 1994. As a bonus, the reader gets posters and yearly introductions from the author, detailing the creative process, the source of inspiration and wacky anecdotes related to the series. I've spaced out my lecture over almost a whole year, in order to prolong the pleasure and avoid 'overeating' a favourite 'dish', yet the first thing I did when I ended was to go back to the beginning and re-read a couple of early 'months'. I would say "The Complete Far Side" is a keeper, a manual of life-hacks guaranteed to pull you out of a funk and to make you look at your troubles and worries from a different angle. What's Larson's secret? How does he do it?<br /><br />A few examples of his comic panels would be self-explanatory, as in the old adage that a picture paints a thousand words, but the artist has kindly requested that his art should not be made freely available on the interwebs. Actually, this makes my task easier, because I would find it impossible to narrow down my favorites to the limited space granted by Goodreads. <br /><br /><i> No live organism can continue for long to exist sanely under conditions of absolute reality </i> explains Shirley Jackson in the opening paragraph of her classic horror "The Haunting of Hill House" . Well, that's what Gary Larson does here : he keeps us sane by taking us on a trip to the wild side of reality. He's the jester who dares to shout out that The Emperor is naked, that his new clothes are a hoax; the stand-up artist that mocks us for hiding with our heads down in the sand, pretending that global warming is a hoax, that the wildlife is not facing extinction, that our jobs are interesting and rewarding, that our politicians are honest or that our kids will have a better life that ours. Again, how does he do it?<br /><br />By turning everything we know down on its head, upside-down and sideways, holding up a mirror of black humour and practical jokes to demonstrate that humanity does not deserve its place at the top of the food chain, that our pets are watching us and judging us, that animals in the forest are out to get us, aliens are laughing their heads off at our antics, scientists are as clueless and prone to eraser fights as kids in school, that even amoebas, flies and ticks like to sit in a comfy chair in the evening, reading the papers and gossiping about the neighbours.<br /><br /><i> Sugar Plum Fairy came and hit the streets<br />Lookin' for soul food and a place to eat<br />Went to the Apollo<br />You should have seen him go, go, go<br />They said, hey Sugar, take a walk on the wild side<br />I said, hey babe, take a walk on the wild side, alright, huh </i><br /> [Lou Reed]<br /><br />Some people like to let the Holy Book fall open and find wisdom by randomly pointing a finger at one of the stanzas. I would rather find my answers by picking a new Farside cartoon each day. If ever I am stranded on a desert island, or visiting a cannibal village, if deers suddenly start knocking on my door or crocodiles invite me to a cocktail party, if aliens ask me directions to the nearest fast-food restaurant or if monsters are lurking under my bed, if I'm confused about rocket science, art, prehistory or politics - I know what to do and what to say to them : Go visit the Farside! All you need is to leave your prejudices behind, get in touch with your inner child and enjoy the cowpocalypse!<br /><br />Thank you, Mr. Larson for redeeming my faith in the future. It may be a future without humans, with bugs, cows, ducks and dogs (but not cats) taking over the planet, but life does go on in unexpected directions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17662591480732151455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_406862855" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406862855" />
    <a title="Chrisl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11928354-chrisl"><img alt="Chrisl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604643214p2/11928354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406862855?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrisl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrisl" href="/user/show/11928354-chrisl">Chrisl</a>
      </span>

  <span id="freeText15645522894904791514" style="display:none">I've loved The Far Side since my first brush with it. My local paper used to publish a lovely, full color comic book with their Sunday edition. Alas, it's gone now. If there's anything in the Sunday paper of the same quality as The Far Side or Calvin and Hobbes, I would dearly like to know about it. <br /><br />At any rate, I always loved The Far Side, though I didn't always understand it. Like so many other childhood memories, there's always the question of if it'll hold up when revisited. Not a problem here. Like I said, I didn't understand every Far Side comic back then, and I think I got it now. Funny, irreverent, cheerfully strange, and full of cows. It's still second only to Calvin and Hobbes in my affections, and that's some lofty company to keep in my eyes. <br /><br />(Note: My local library only had volume one for some reason (?) so I still need to get my hands on volume two to finish.)</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1191018-dale?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287164184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12140504648910519421">Like most techies of the 80s I was a huge fan of <i>The Far Side</i>. It is pretty surprising how many of these panels I still remember after nearly 30 years: they must have made quite an impression. And some of them can still make me snort laugh (and, really, I almost never snort laugh).<br/><br/>The collection contains a few of the complaint letters received by the newspapers that carried the strip: people complainging about the "poor taste" of some of the cartoons; or complaining because Larson had strips abo</span>
  <span id="freeText12140504648910519421" style="display:none">Like most techies of the 80s I was a huge fan of <i>The Far Side</i>. It is pretty surprising how many of these panels I still remember after nearly 30 years: they must have made quite an impression. And some of them can still make me snort laugh (and, really, I almost never snort laugh).<br /><br />The collection contains a few of the complaint letters received by the newspapers that carried the strip: people complainging about the "poor taste" of some of the cartoons; or complaining because Larson had strips about hell (aerobics in hell, dog hell, etc.), and Christians don't want that, naturally; or "think of the children". The letters are so outraged or pompous that they are funny in their own right.<br /><br />My only complaint about the book is that is so very large: it is quite difficult to hold for any length of time!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12140504648910519421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_29438070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29438070" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1341349-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440719801p2/1341349.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29438070?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/1341349-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Scientists, people with a strange sense of humour</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1341349-john?shelf=comics-and-graphic-novels">comics-and-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1341349-john?shelf=books-i-read-as-a-kid">books-i-read-as-a-kid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1341349-john?shelf=all-time-favourite-books">all-time-favourite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29438070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5537193492168594165">This belongs on the shelf with my ‘Complete Calvin and Hobbes’ collection. This set is beautifully designed and presented. Gary Larson's cartoons are brilliantly perverse and funny. Larson is an artist/cartoonist who is never afraid to challenge his readers, and his ‘Far Side’ is a collection of the strange, the bizarre and the downright weird. I particularly like the fact that he sides most often with the animals he portrays more so than the humans (another similarity with Calvin and Hobbes) an</span>
  <span id="freeText5537193492168594165" style="display:none">This belongs on the shelf with my ‘Complete Calvin and Hobbes’ collection. This set is beautifully designed and presented. Gary Larson's cartoons are brilliantly perverse and funny. Larson is an artist/cartoonist who is never afraid to challenge his readers, and his ‘Far Side’ is a collection of the strange, the bizarre and the downright weird. I particularly like the fact that he sides most often with the animals he portrays more so than the humans (another similarity with Calvin and Hobbes) and how he often uses animals acting like people to show us just how silly we are. <br /><br />So why doesn’t it get 5 stars like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24812.The_Complete_Calvin_and_Hobbes" title="The Complete Calvin and Hobbes by Bill Watterson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Complete Calvin and Hobbes</a>? Well the simple answer is that while the Calvin and Hobbes set includes every Calvin and Hobbes strip, poem and short story ever penned, the ‘Complete’ Far Side only includes every strip ever published in the papers, so all the extras from the books, like the story, ‘The Curse of Madame C’ or Larson’s collection of ‘Wiener dog Art’ are missing! This really bugs me every time I read through it. Here we have a stunning collection and it’s incomplete. It’s like someone went out of their way to ruin a potentially awesome collection for no discernable reason. If they ever publish a fully complete Far Side collection like this, I’ll have to sell this copy and buy the better one. Until then, this keeps the 4 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5537193492168594165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer164754640" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11388854562232920054">This compendium weighs a ton. No kidding.<br/>A delightfully inspired packaging of "all things FAR SIDE" from the looney talking cows all the way to conspiratorial chipmunks. Wonderfully packaged but very, very, very expensive, this two volume set includes occasional essays (yes, I said essays) from the genius Larson himself covering such items of the nature of "what I was thinking when I drew ___" to "gosh, I'm sure sorry this thing is going to weigh so much." Of course, there's no apology for the p</span>
  <span id="freeText11388854562232920054" style="display:none">This compendium weighs a ton. No kidding.<br />A delightfully inspired packaging of "all things FAR SIDE" from the looney talking cows all the way to conspiratorial chipmunks. Wonderfully packaged but very, very, very expensive, this two volume set includes occasional essays (yes, I said essays) from the genius Larson himself covering such items of the nature of "what I was thinking when I drew ___" to "gosh, I'm sure sorry this thing is going to weigh so much." Of course, there's no apology for the price (snicker, snicker), but, having grown up on his simplistic renderings of single panel humor, I have to admit that this collection is honestly worth every penny.<br /><br />The best two-volume investment I've ever made, THE FAR SIDE should be required reading for high school graduation, as far as I'm concerned. <br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer655943436315375908">Love love love The Far Side. It has long been my favorite comic strip. Back in the early 90s I used to clip the daily cartoon out of the newspaper and collect them. Later I enjoyed several years of the daily calendar.<br/><br/>I have learned one thing from reading this collection, though. The Far Side is best enjoyed a little at a time, and for me isn't as good when reading through dozens of cartoons in one sitting. I began to notice certain themes or jokes that recurred in various cartoons, for example.<br/><br/>F</span>
  <span id="freeText655943436315375908" style="display:none">Love love love The Far Side. It has long been my favorite comic strip. Back in the early 90s I used to clip the daily cartoon out of the newspaper and collect them. Later I enjoyed several years of the daily calendar.<br /><br />I have learned one thing from reading this collection, though. The Far Side is best enjoyed a little at a time, and for me isn't as good when reading through dozens of cartoons in one sitting. I began to notice certain themes or jokes that recurred in various cartoons, for example.<br /><br />Five stars for being what it is. Just take your time getting through it. The Far Side was created as a daily strip and works better when consumed that way.</span>

There are dozens of head-scratchers in here (and I'm reasonably intelligent), a few duds and hundreds of laugh-out-loud funny comics. My only complaint is that there's just too much. Better to leaf through on a cold winter afternoon than sit down and try to bomb through the whole thing at once.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2313247596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313247596" />
    <a title="Dominick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5913578-dominick"><img alt="Dominick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443184611p2/5913578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313247596?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominick" href="/user/show/5913578-dominick">Dominick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781449460044" href="/book/show/22668916-the-complete-far-side">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913578-dominick?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913578-dominick?shelf=cartoons">cartoons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313247596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5612806304109676654">I'm dinging this a star for presentation. Often, there are three or even four strips a page, which, even in this oversize format, means that some strips are printed at smaller than their original size which wasn't generous to begin with). I get that even so the book is over 1200 pages long, so there were practical reasons for such a decision, but it nevertheless impacts negatively on the reading experience. Otherwise, it's hard to complain about a comprehensive collection of one of the great fun</span>
  <span id="freeText5612806304109676654" style="display:none">I'm dinging this a star for presentation. Often, there are three or even four strips a page, which, even in this oversize format, means that some strips are printed at smaller than their original size which wasn't generous to begin with). I get that even so the book is over 1200 pages long, so there were practical reasons for such a decision, but it nevertheless impacts negatively on the reading experience. Otherwise, it's hard to complain about a comprehensive collection of one of the great funny (if often bizarre and occasionally incomprehensible) one-panel strips. Even having read all the previous collections, I found I did not recognize or remember many strips here, either because they were previously uncollected, or just because I simply forgot about them. Either way, the effect was sort of like discovering a trove of new <i>Far Side</i> strips, and that's a good thing. There is occasional editorial and contextualizing material (e.g. a short introduction for each year's worth of strips, or occasional reproduced letters from baffled or offended readers--sometimes with responses), but I'd have liked to see more of this, as well. One can only imagine how many letters from irate and/or baffled readers remain unreproduced. And given how Larson pushed the envelope (even now, I was surprised when I hit the first cartoon about sperm and an ovum), a history of objections to the strip might be fascinating. Nevertheless, this is all the strips, about which one really can't complain. Essential for any fan of weird humour, especially in cartoon form.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5612806304109676654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2397278933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2397278933" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5328642-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431263789p2/5328642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2397278933?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/5328642-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781449460044" href="/book/show/22668916-the-complete-far-side">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2397278933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1578693483746012637">On the one hand, I love Larson's wry, sometimes obscure sense of humor (this edition includes several letters from readers begging him to explain specific comics). His art style is one of my all time favorites in the world of comic strips. On the other hand, this kind of compendium does his comics a disservice. They are, it seems, best suited to the kind of one-a-day format one gets from the newspaper or even a desk calendar. Seeing/reading them all in succession like this I was able to pick up </span>
  <span id="freeText1578693483746012637" style="display:none">On the one hand, I love Larson's wry, sometimes obscure sense of humor (this edition includes several letters from readers begging him to explain specific comics). His art style is one of my all time favorites in the world of comic strips. On the other hand, this kind of compendium does his comics a disservice. They are, it seems, best suited to the kind of one-a-day format one gets from the newspaper or even a desk calendar. Seeing/reading them all in succession like this I was able to pick up on repeated jokes and it made them seem staler overall. For instance, I counted 5 Humpty Dumpty comics, which all boil down to "he died after he fell off the wall," and more desert island comics than I can remember. Now, this isn't to say that he wasn't creative or that he isn't funny, only that this format does not work as well for him as it does the more narrative-based comics like Calvin &amp; Hobbes or Fox Trot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1578693483746012637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2248257516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2248257516" />
    <a title="Sheri-lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3110230-sheri-lee"><img alt="Sheri-lee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheri-lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheri-lee" href="/user/show/3110230-sheri-lee">Sheri-lee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2248257516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18283349126334085594">Gary Larson was an innovator. On the edge of ‘the fine line’ sometimes, weird, odd ball, and satiric. I hated that the odd time there would be one I didn’t get ... I feel like (probably smugly) there is a certain amount of smarts required to fully enjoy The Far Side and I didn’t like feeling I didn’t have those smarts. I will say that the majority of his comics are awesome, but I especially love the ones that catch you by surprise and make you snicker or spit laugh out loud. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2108500402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2108500402" />
    <a title="Anjan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12536207-anjan"><img alt="Anjan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364871428p2/12536207.jpg" /></a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2108500402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15812333895117541010">Because this is a complete set, you'll be easily able to pick up on variations of theme. Old west, islands, deserts, fish out of water, people in water, cows, etc. As I flipped through the pages I'd sometimes feel as if I could set up a 3 axis model with elements of the comics and predict what I would come upon next. Which isn't to say he was repeating himself (though sometimes it felt repetitive). <br/><br/> <br/><br/></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_265115070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265115070" />
    <a title="Xavier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7434761-xavier"><img alt="Xavier" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265115070?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xavier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xavier" href="/user/show/7434761-xavier">Xavier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265115070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6550465457850834930">One of the better comics series drawn to date, The Far Side's brand of humor cannot be imitated. It's not dark (early comics notwithstanding) so much as it is slightly twisted. It offers perspectives on science from Neanderthals, pranks from cows, and rather blasé reactions to bizarre, freakish accidents and incidents. It seems to come directly from some deep part of the human psyche that takes joy when things add up wrongly. There's no real way to describe what's going on in this book, but it's</span>
  <span id="freeText6550465457850834930" style="display:none">One of the better comics series drawn to date, The Far Side's brand of humor cannot be imitated. It's not dark (early comics notwithstanding) so much as it is slightly twisted. It offers perspectives on science from Neanderthals, pranks from cows, and rather blasé reactions to bizarre, freakish accidents and incidents. It seems to come directly from some deep part of the human psyche that takes joy when things add up wrongly. There's no real way to describe what's going on in this book, but it's highly entertaining wether it's dealing in absurdity or wit. Commentary and hate mail breathe fresh life into some of the weaker comics. If you're considering owning Gary Larson's comics, I'd recommend getting the complete works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6550465457850834930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1322981151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322981151" />
    <a title="CartoonistAndre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22327959-cartoonistandre"><img alt="CartoonistAndre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417744723p2/22327959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322981151?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CartoonistAndre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CartoonistAndre" href="/user/show/22327959-cartoonistandre">CartoonistAndre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322981151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4097812901414269420">I can't think of one more funny and 'complete' cartoonist. His name would be at the top of my list. Although his earlier artwork seemed juvenile, unrefined, but very insightful and funny, those quirky characters with slits for eyes or an "o" for a mouth became a contemporary classic legend. His 'rudimentary' style worked perfectly with his extraordinary sense of absurdity. Admittedly there were some panels that could seem 'over the top' for many sensitive minds but the man is legend and began a </span>
  <span id="freeText4097812901414269420" style="display:none">I can't think of one more funny and 'complete' cartoonist. His name would be at the top of my list. Although his earlier artwork seemed juvenile, unrefined, but very insightful and funny, those quirky characters with slits for eyes or an "o" for a mouth became a contemporary classic legend. His 'rudimentary' style worked perfectly with his extraordinary sense of absurdity. Admittedly there were some panels that could seem 'over the top' for many sensitive minds but the man is legend and began a style that has affected so many of today's top inkslingers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4097812901414269420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524585589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6694245747160986486">As I believe most fans were, I was pretty sad when Gary Larson put up his pen for good. This incredible set includes all of his Far Side comics in 2 beautiful hardback books 3x thicker than most coffee table books (each). I bought it as soon as it came out and dove in. I go back and read them all at least once a year, his cartoons have made me laugh til my sides hurt sometimes, and I'm so glad they came out with this. ... I just wish it came with a Hunky man to lug it around for me ;)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JOXPbNWs+8qO9EV7LSQgGgoJcT9EI434iLFKOGrwXyBOKuFKNlTIKcd6O25zmiGwNMeUZlgJah6dhPd5VqV/vQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KPKhYkwCav6yIHNsRLCEvZEWfUt7e6jfDMX+W+dDUYNCPY9Er/pZHfuuDXkaDoUXr9iYEmdRTzkZ8EMa2xZxHg==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_24812'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24812.The_Complete_Calvin_and_Hobbes?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Complete Calvin and Hobbes<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/13778.Bill_Watterson?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Bill Watterson<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><\/span> 4.82 avg rating &mdash; 35,054 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2005\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer4296750656867395727\">[ \n  Box Set\n | Book One | Book Two | Book Three ]\n\nCalvin and Hobbes is unquestionably one of the most popular comic strips of all time. The imaginative world of a boy and his real-only-to-him tiger was first syndicated in 1985 and appeared in more <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4296750656867395727\" style=\"display:none\">[ \n  Box Set\n | Book One | Book Two | Book Three ]\n\nCalvin and Hobbes is unquestionably one of the most popular comic strips of all time. The imaginative world of a boy and his real-only-to-him tiger was first syndicated in 1985 and appeared in more than 2,400 newspapers when Bill Watterson retired on January 1, 1996.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/19928.Gary_Larson">About Gary Larson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/19928.Gary_Larson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1213672623p3/19928.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/19928.Gary_Larson">Gary Larson
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7929469228694730797">Gary Larson was born and raised in Tacoma, Washington. His parents were Vern, a car salesman, and Doris, a secretary. He attended Curtis High School before attending Washington State University and graduated in 1972 with a degree in communications. In 1987, Larson married Toni Carmichael, an archaeologist.<br/><br/>Larson credits his older brother Dan for his "paranoid" sense of humor. Dan would pull countl</span>
  <span id="freeText7929469228694730797" style="display:none">Gary Larson was born and raised in Tacoma, Washington. His parents were Vern, a car salesman, and Doris, a secretary. He attended Curtis High School before attending Washington State University and graduated in 1972 with a degree in communications. In 1987, Larson married Toni Carmichael, an archaeologist.<br /><br />Larson credits his older brother Dan for his "paranoid" sense of humor. Dan would pull countless pranks on Gary, taking advantage of his phobia of monsters under the bed by, for example, waiting in the closet for the right moment to pounce out at Gary. Dan is also credited with giving Gary his love of science. They caught animals in Puget Sound and placed them in terrariums in the basement; even making a small desert ecosystem, which their parents apparently did not mind. His adept use of snakes in his cartoons stems from his long-standing interest in herpetology.<br />Since retiring from the Far Side, Larson has occasionally done some cartooning work, such as magazine illustrations and promotional artwork for Far Side merchandise.<br /><br />In 1998, Larson published his first post-Far Side book, There's a Hair in My Dirt!: A Worm's Story, an illustrated story with the unmistakable Far Side mindset.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7929469228694730797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
